        "tool_use_id": "toolu_01MtyYJywVGktE4Q24AqsUT8",
        "type": "tool_result",
        "content": "# ForkUnion: Overview and Integration Guide\n\n## What Is ForkUnion?\n\nForkUnion is \"the lowest-latency OpenMP-style NUMA-aware minimalistic scoped thread-pool designed for 'Fork-Join' parallelism in C++, C, and Rust.\" It avoids mutexes, dynamic memory allocations, CAS-primitives, and false-sharing on the critical path.\n\n## Core APIs\n\n**Basic Operations:**\n- `try_spawn()` - initializes worker threads\n- `for_threads()` - launches a blocking callback on all threads\n- `for_n()` - distributes evenly-sized tasks across threads\n- `for_n_dynamic()` - distributes unevenly-sized tasks with work-stealing\n- `for_slices()` - distributes slice-based tasks\n\n**Additional Helpers:**\n- `sleep(microseconds)` - implements longer pauses\n- `terminate()` - stops threads before destructor\n- `unsafe_for_threads()` and `unsafe_join()` - advanced flow control\n\n## C++ Integration\n\n**Three integration approaches:**\n\n1. **Direct inclusion**: Copy `include/fork_union.hpp` into your project\n2. **Git submodule**: `git submodule add https://github.com/ashvardanian/fork_union.git extern/fork_union`\n3. **CMake FetchContent**:\n```cpp\nFetchContent_Declare(fork_union \n  GIT_REPOSITORY https://github.com/ashvardanian/fork_union\n  GIT_TAG v2.3.0)\nFetchContent_MakeAvailable(fork_union)\ntarget_link_libraries(your_target PRIVATE fork_union::fork_union)\n```\n\n## Key Classes\n\n- `basic_pool_t` - fundamental thread pool implementation\n- `linux_colocated_pool` - NUMA-aware variant (Linux only)\n- `linux_distributed_pool_t` - balances work across NUMA nodes\n- `linux_numa_allocator` - allocates memory on specific NUMA nodes\n- `spin_mutex_t` - lightweight alternative to `std::mutex`\n\n## Design Philosophy\n\nThe library prioritizes performance by eliminating costly synchronization primitives on the execution path, making it ideal for fine-grained parallelism and Big Data applications where predictable, low-latency performance matters."
      }

      {
        "tool_use_id": "toolu_01TnLX9mqqja6nmWC5ymJnmo",
        "type": "tool_result",
        "content": "# ForkUnion Usage Examples\n\n## Initialization\n\nThe library provides a straightforward initialization pattern:\n\n```cpp\n#include <fork_union.hpp>\n\nusing fu = ashvardanian::fork_union;\n\nfu::basic_pool_t pool;\nif (!pool.try_spawn(std::thread::hardware_concurrency()))\n    return EXIT_FAILURE;\n```\n\nThe `try_spawn()` method accepts thread count and an optional exclusivity parameter (`caller_inclusive_k` by default).\n\n## Parallel Task Execution\n\n### Thread Broadcasting (`for_threads`)\n\nExecute a function across all threads:\n\n```cpp\npool.for_threads([](std::size_t thread_id) noexcept {\n    std::printf(\"Hi from thread %zu\\n\", thread_id);\n});\n```\n\n### Indexed Loops (`for_n`)\n\nDistribute N similar-duration tasks:\n\n```cpp\npool.for_n(100, [](auto prong) noexcept {\n    auto [task_index, thread_index] = prong;\n    // Process task at task_index\n});\n```\n\n### Dynamic Workload (`for_n_dynamic`)\n\nHandle uneven task durations with work-stealing:\n\n```cpp\npool.for_n_dynamic(1000, [](auto prong) noexcept {\n    auto [task_index, thread_index] = prong;\n    // Process variable-duration task\n});\n```\n\n### Slice-Based Distribution (`for_slices`)\n\nProcess contiguous ranges instead of individual indices:\n\n```cpp\npool.for_slices(100, [](auto prong, std::size_t slice_length) noexcept {\n    auto [first_index, thread_id] = prong;\n    for (std::size_t i = 0; i < slice_length; ++i)\n        process(first_index + i);\n});\n```\n\n## Key Method Signatures\n\n- `bool try_spawn(thread_count, exclusivity = caller_inclusive_k)`\n- `void for_threads(lambda_callback)`\n- `void for_n(count, lambda_callback)`\n- `void for_n_dynamic(count, lambda_callback)`\n- `void for_slices(count, lambda_callback)`\n- `void terminate()`\n\nAll callbacks must be **noexcept** functions."
      }
    ]
  },

The benchmark script (`examples/benchmark.sh`) can be used to measure performance improvements for different workloads.\n\nExample usage:\n```bash\n# Create archive with 4 threads\nbar a archive.bar files/ -j 4\n\n# Extract with 8 threads\nbar x archive.bar -o output/ -j 8\n\n# Single-threaded mode (for comparison)\nbar a archive.bar files/ -j 1\n```\n\n### Acceptance Criteria Status\n\n- ‚úÖ The `add` and `extract` commands support parallelism with measurable speedup\n- ‚úÖ Parallelism level is controllable via the `-j/--threads` flag  \n- ‚úÖ All existing functionality continues to work (backward compatible)\n- ‚úÖ Implementation is thread-safe with proper synchronization\n\nFixes #5\n\nü§ñ Generated with [Claude Code](https://claude.com/claude-code)\nEOF\n)\" 2>&1",

A bit within this field could signal the presence of an optional, extended header immediately following the standard one. This extended header could contain information necessary for parallel processing, such as an offset to the next entry.\\n\\nIf this approach proves insufficient, a full redesign of `header_t` should be considered.\\n\\n\\n**Acceptance Criteria**\\n\\n- The `add` and `extract` commands demonstrate significant, measurable speedup on multi-core systems.\\n- The level of parallelism is controllable via the new `-j`/`--threads` flag.\\n- All existing tests and benchmarks continue to pass.\\n- The implementation is thread-safe and robust against race conditions.\",\"comments\":[],\"title\":\"Parallel archiving and extraction using `ForkUnion`\"}",

a/extern/fork_union/include/fork_union.hpp b/extern/fork_union/include/fork_union.hpp\n   124‚Üínew file mode 100644\n   125‚Üíindex 0000000..cf2ab2f\n   126‚Üí--- /dev/null\n   127‚Üí+++ b/extern/fork_union/include/fork_union.hpp\n   128‚Üí@@ -0,0 +1,4073 @@\n   129‚Üí+/**\n   130‚Üí+ *  @brief  Low-latency OpenMP-style NUMA-aware cross-platform fine-grained parallelism library.\n   131‚Üí+ *  @file   fork_union.hpp\n   132‚Üí+ *  @author Ash Vardanian\n   133‚Üí+ *  @date   May 2, 2025\n   134‚Üí+ *\n   135‚Üí+ *  Fork Union provides a minimalistic cross-platform thread-pool implementation and Parallel Algorithms,\n   136‚Üí+ *  avoiding dynamic memory allocations, exceptions, system calls, and heavy Compare-And-Swap instructions.\n   137‚Üí+ *  The library leverages the \"weak memory model\" to allow Arm and IBM Power CPUs to aggressively optimize\n   138‚Üí+ *  execution at runtime. It also aggressively tests against overflows on smaller index types, and is safe\n   139‚Üí+ *  to use even with the maximal `std::size_t` values.\n   140‚Üí+ *\n   141‚Üí+ *  @code{.cpp}\n   142‚Üí+ *  #include <cstdio> // `std::printf`\n   143‚Üí+ *  #include <cstdlib> // `EXIT_FAILURE`, `EXIT_SUCCESS`\n   144‚Üí+ *  #include <fork_union.hpp> // `fu::basic_pool_t`\n   145‚Üí+ *\n   146‚Üí+ *  using fu = ashvardanian::fork_union;\n   147‚Üí+ *  int main(int argc, char *argv[]) {\n   148‚Üí+ *\n   149‚Üí+ *      fu::basic_pool_t pool;\n   150‚Üí+ *      if (!pool.try_spawn(std::thread::hardware_concurrency()))\n   151‚Üí+ *          return EXIT_FAILURE;\n   152‚Üí+ *\n   153‚Üí+ *      pool.for_n(argc, [=](auto prong) noexcept {\n   154‚Üí+ *          auto [task_index, thread_index, colocation_index] = prong;\n   155‚Üí+ *          std::printf(\n   156‚Üí+ *              \"Printing argument # %zu (of %zu) from thread # %zu at colocation # %zu: %s\\n\",\n   157‚Üí+ *              task_index, argc, thread_index, colocation_index, argv[task_index]);\n   158‚Üí+ *      });\n   159‚Üí+ *      return EXIT_SUCCESS;\n   160‚Üí+ *  }\n   161‚Üí+ *  @endcode\n   162‚Üí+ *\n   163‚Üí+ *  The next layer of logic is for basic index-addressable tasks. It includes basic parallel loops:\n   164‚Üí+ *\n   165‚Üí+ *  - `for_n` - for iterating over a range of similar duration tasks, addressable by an index.\n   166‚Üí+ *  - `for_n_dynamic` - for unevenly distributed tasks, where each task may take a different time.\n   167‚Üí+ *  - `for_slices` - for iterating over a range of similar duration tasks, addressable by a slice.\n   168‚Üí+ *\n   169‚Üí+ *  ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n   170‚Üí+ *\n   171‚Üí+ *  On Linux, when NUMA and PThreads are available, the library can also leverage @b NUMA-aware\n   172‚Üí+ *  memory allocations and pin threads to specific physical cores to increase memory locality.\n   173‚Üí+ *  It should reduce memory access latency by around 35% on average, compared to remote accesses.\n   174‚Üí+ *  @sa `numa_topology_t`, `linux_colocated_pool_t`, `linux_distributed_pool_t`.\n   175‚Üí+ *\n   176‚Üí+ *  On heterogeneous chips, cores with a different @b \"Quality-of-Service\" (QoS) may be combined.\n   177‚Üí+ *  A typical example is laptop/desktop chips, having 1 NUMA node, but 3 tiers of CPU cores:\n   178‚Üí+ *  performance, efficiency, and power-saving cores. Each group will have vastly different speed,\n   179‚Üí+ *  so considering them equal in tasks scheduling is a bad idea... and separating them automatically\n   180‚Üí+ *  isn't feasible either. It's up to the user to isolate those groups into individual pools.\n   181‚Üí+ *  @sa `qos_level_t`\n   182‚Üí+ *\n   183‚Üí+ *  On x86, Arm, and RISC-V (internally referred to as RISC5) architectures, depending on the CPU\n   184‚Üí+ *  features available, the library also exposes cheaper @b \"busy-waiting\" mechanisms, such as\n   185‚Üí+ *  `tpause`, `wfet`, & `yield` instructions.\n   186‚Üí+ *  @sa `arm64_yield_t`, `arm64_wfet_t`, `x86_yield_t`, `x86_tpause_t`, `risc5_yield_t`.\n   187‚Üí+ *\n   188‚Üí+ *  The library uses modern C++ features and requires @b C++17 or newer.\n   189‚Üí+ *  Using C++20 will enable additional compile-time checks (concepts) where available.\n   190‚Üí+ */\n   191‚Üí+#pragma once\n   192‚Üí+#if defined(_MSC_VER)\n   193‚Üí+#pragma warning(disable : 4505) // unreferenced function with internal linkage has been removed\n   194‚Üí+#pragma warning(disable : 4324) // structure was padded due to alignment specifier\n
